## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt typically depends on restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v), and possibly external driving (functions of t). The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, damping, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Pendulum-like oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (pendulum with damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Quadratic-cubic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodically driven)
- Nonlinear damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Morse-type oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * x) * (1 - exp(c1 * x)) (asymmetric potential well)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power terms in position (x²) → asymmetric potential wells causing drift or asymmetric oscillations
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x²)*v → self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles) as in Van der Pol
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) → bounded restoring force allowing unbounded motion beyond a threshold (pendulum-like)
- Cubic position terms with opposite sign to linear term (c0*x - c1*x³) → double-well potential with bistability
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous/conservative system; presence of sin/cos(t) → driven system with possible resonance
- Products of x and v (x*v terms) → energy-dependent damping or nonlinear coupling between position and momentum
- Negative linear velocity coefficient with positive nonlinear velocity terms → amplitude-dependent damping leading to limit cycles
